138. ‘sew’: *<i>si̯eu̯</i>- (: Lat. <i>suere</i>, -<i>ō</i>, Lith. <i>siuvù</i>, <i>siū´ti</i>, Skt. <i>sī́vyati</i>, Goth. <i>siujan</i>, CSl. <i>šijǫ</i>, <i>šiti</i>). LIV 545, IEW 915 f., EIEC 569 ff.

139. ‘count’:? *<i>reh₁</i>- ‘reckon, count’ only in Lat. <i>reor</i>, <i>ratus sum</i>, <i>ratio</i> ‘counting, reason’ and Goth. <i>raþjo</i> ‘number, counting’. IEW 59, LIV 499; EIEC 397.

140. ‘say’: ‘say, speak’: *<i>mleu̯h₂-</i> (: Skt. <i>brávīti</i> ‘says’, OAv. <i>mraomī</i>, Cz. <i>mluviti</i> ‘speak’, Russ. <i>molvá</i> ‘rumour’, Toch. B <i>palwaṃ</i> ‘laments’). LIV 446, IEW −; *<i>h₂u̯ed</i>-(: Skt. <i>vádati</i>, Gk. <i>audē´</i> ‘voice’, <i>audáō</i> ‘I speak’, Hitt. <i>watarnah̬h̬</i>- ‘command’). LIV 286, IEW 76 f.; *<i>sekᵘ̯</i>- (: Gk. <i>ennépō</i>, Lat. <i>inquit</i> ‘said’, <i>insece</i> ‘tell!’, Lith. <i>sekù</i>, <i>sèkti</i> ‘tell’, <i>sakaũ</i>, <i>sakýti</i> ‘say’, ON <i>segja</i> ‘say’, NE <i>say</i>). LIV 526, IEW 897 f., probably related to→ *<i>sekᵘ̯</i>- ‘follow’ [212] (*‘follow up with words’); *<i>bʰeh2-</i> (probably identical with *<i>bʰeh2-</i> ‘shine’ [246] via ‘make clear’: Gk. <i>pʰēmí</i>, Arm. <i>bam</i>, Lat. <i>for</i>, <i>fārī</i>, ORuss. <i>baju</i>, <i>bajati</i> ‘tell’; Skt. <i>bhánati</i>). LIV 69, IEW 105 f.; *<i>u̯ekᵘ̯</i>- (: Skt. [aor.] <i>ávocat</i>, Av. -<i>vaocat̰</i> Gk. <i>eĩpon</i>, cf. noun *<i>u̯ōkᵘ̯</i>-<i>s</i> ‘voice’ in Lat. <i>vōx</i>, Skt. <i>vāc</i>-, gr. <i>op</i>-). LIV 673, IEW 1135 f.; *<i>u̯erh₁</i>- (: Pal. <i>wērti</i> ‘speaks’, Hitt. particle of quotation -<i>wa[r]</i>, prs. <i>weriyezzi</i> ‘calls’, Gk. <i>eírō</i>, Russ. <i>vru</i>, <i>vrat’</i> ‘lie’). LIV 689 f., IEW 1162 f.; *<i>h₂eg̑</i>- (: Lat. <i>aiō</i>, Arm. <i>asem</i>, Gk. [impf.] <i>ē˜</i> ‘said’, [pf.] <i>ánōga</i> ‘I command’, Toch. B [subj.] <i>āksạ̈ṃ</i> ‘I will proclaim’). LIV 256, IEW 290 f.; *<i>ter</i>- (: Hitt. <i>taranzi</i> [3pl. in suppletion with 3sg <i>tezzi</i> from PIE → *<i>dʰ</i>eh₁- ‘place, put’ [224] > ‘say’], Lith. <i>tariù</i>, <i>tarýti</i>). LIV 630 f., IEW 1088 f., EIEC 534 ff. → ‘speak solemly, vow’ [254].

141. ‘sing’: *<i>geH(i)</i>- (: Skt. <i>gā´yati</i>, ORuss. <i>gaju</i>, <i>gajati</i> ‘creak’, Lith. <i>gíedu</i>, <i>giedóti</i>). LIV 183, IEW 355; *<i>sengᵘ̯ʰ</i>- (: Goth. <i>siggwan</i>, probably Gk. [aor.] <i>eápʰtʰē</i> ‘resounded’, OCS <i>sętъ</i> ‘says’). LIV 532, IEW 906 f.; *<i>h₁erkᵘ̯</i>- ‘shine; sing’ (: Hitt. <i>arkuwanzi</i> [3pl.] ‘sing’, Skt. <i>árcati</i> ‘shines; sings’, Toch. A <i>yärksantär</i> [3pl.] ‘worship’; cf. also OIr. <i>erc</i> ‘sky’ and Arm. <i>erg</i> ‘song’, probably a metaphor ‘shining song’, cf. Gk. <i>paiā´n lámpei</i> ‘the song of praise shines’, <i>húmnoi pʰlégonti</i> ‘the hymns shine’, cf. Mayrhofer 2006: s.v. <i>ARC</i>). LIV 240 f., IEW 340, EIEC 519 f. → ‘shine’ [246].

142. ‘play’: It is unclear if the concept of ‘play’ existed for speakers of PIE. *<i>lei̯d</i>-, from which Lat. <i>lūdus</i> ‘game’, <i>lūdere</i>, -<i>ō</i> ‘play’ and Gk. (Hsch.) <i>lízei</i> ‘plays’, <i>loidoréō</i> ‘I insult’ are derived, probably meant ‘let go’ originally, cf. OLith. <i>léidmi</i> (later <i>léidžiu</i>), <i>léisti</i> ‘let go, impel’, MIr. <i>láidid</i> ‘impels, drives on’, Alb. <i>lind</i> ‘is born’ (*‘is let go’). LIV 402 f., IEW 666, EIEC 434.

143. ‘float’: cf. [119].

144. ‘flow’: *<i>sreu̯</i>- (: Skt. <i>srávati</i>, Gk. <i>rʰéō</i>, Lith. <i>sraviù</i>, <i>sravė́ti</i>, Arm. <i>ar̄oganem</i>, <i>or̄oganem</i> ‘I irrigate’). LIV 588, IEW 1003, NIL 630 ff. cf. also [119]; *<i>gᵘ̯g̑ʰer</i>- (: Skt. <i>kṣárati</i>, YAv. <i>fra</i>-<i>žgaraiti</i>, Gk. <i>pʰtʰeíromai</i> ‘I shipwreck; perish’, Toch. B [3pl.] <i>kwreṃntär</i> ‘grow old, weak’). LIV 213 f., IEW 487 f.

145. ‘freeze’:?*<i>sreiHgʰ</i>- (: Gk. <i>érʰrʰīga</i> [pf.] ‘I freeze, tremble [with cold]’, <i>rʰīgéō</i> ‘id.’, Lat. <i>frīgēre</i>, -<i>eō</i> ‘be cold, freeze’). Only Greek and Latin. LIV 587 f., IEW1004.

146. ‘swell’: *<i>h₂ei̯d</i>- (: Arm. <i>aytnowm</i>, Gk. <i>oidéō</i>). LIV 258, IEW 774; *<i>u̯eh₁</i>- (: Skt. <i>śváyati</i>, Gk. <i>kuéō</i> ‘I am pregnant’, Lat. <i>inciēns</i> ‘pregnant’). LIV 339 f., IEW 592–594; *<i>pei̯H</i>- (: Skt. <i>pínvati</i>, YAv. <i>fra</i>-<i>pinaoiti</i>, Lith. <i>pyjù</i>, <i>pýti</i>; → adj. ‘fat’ [66]). LIV 464 f., IEW 793; *<i>teu̯h₂</i>- (: Skt. <i>tavīti</i>, RCS, ORuss. <i>tyju</i>, <i>tyti</i> ‘become fat’). LIV 639 f., IEW 1080 f., EIEC 560 f.

147. ‘sun’: *<i>seh₂u̯el</i>/<i>n</i>-: (: Lat. <i>sōl</i>, Gk. [Hom.] <i>ēélios</i>, Skt. <i>s<sub>ú</sub>var</i>-/<i>sū́rᵢya</i>-, Goth. <i>sauil</i> beside <i>sunnō</i>, Av. <i>huuarə̄</i>, gen. Av. <i>xᵛə̄ṇg</i> < *<i>sh₂u̯en</i>-<i>s</i>, Lith. <i>sáulė</i>, OCS <i>slъnьce</i>, OIr. <i>súil</i> ‘eye’ (< ‘sun’ = ‘eye of the sky’), CLuw. <i>ši(ḫ)wal</i>- ‘lamp<sup>?</sup>, dagger<sup>?</sup>’, hence *<i>seh₂(u̯)-</i>‘burn, sting’?). IEW 881 f., EIEC 556, NIL 606 ff., EIEC 556.

148. ‘month/moon’: *<i>méh₁n̥s</i>, gen. *<i>meh₁nés</i> (: Skt. <i>mā́s</i>- ‘moon’, <i>mā´sa</i>- ‘month’, OAv. <i>mā̊</i>, Gk. <i>mē´n</i>/<i>meís</i>, Lat. <i>mēnsis</i> ‘month’, Goth. <i>mēna</i>, OHG <i>māno</i> ‘moon’, Lith. <i>mė́nuo</i>, Toch. A <i>mañ</i>, B <i>meñe</i> ‘month/moon’). IEW 731 f., EIEC 385.

149. ‘star’: *<i>h₂ster</i>- (: Gk. <i>astē´r</i>, Arm. <i>astł</i>, Skt. <i>star</i>-, Hitt. <i>ḫašterza</i>, Lat. <i>stella</i> < *<i>ster</i><i>lā</i>) probably from *<i>h₂eh₁s-</i> ‘become dry, burn’ as *<i>h₂[h₁]ster</i>-, cf. Pinault 2007. → ‘dry’ [195]. IEW 1027 f., EIEC 543, NIL 348 ff.

150. ‘water’: *<i>u̯ed</i>- (: Hitt. <i>wātar</i>, gen. <i>witenaš</i>, Gk. <i>húdōr</i>, Umbr. <i>utur</i>, Goth. <i>wato</i>, OE <i>wætar</i>, OHG <i>wazzar</i>, OCS <i>voda</i>, Lith. <i>vanduõ</i>; Skt. <i>udan</i>- ‘water, wave’, Lat. <i>unda</i> ‘wave’, Arm. <i>get</i> ‘river’). LIV 658 f., IEW 78 f., NIL 706 ff. → ‘moisten’ [339]; *<i>h₂ekᵘ̯</i>- (: Lat. <i>aqua</i>, Goth. <i>aƕa</i>). IEW 23, EIEC 636 f. → ‘water, river’ [387]; *<i>u̯eh₁</i>- (: Toch. A <i>wär</i>, B. <i>war</i>, ON <i>úr</i> ‘thin rain, moisture’, cLuv. <i>wārša</i>-, Skt. <i>vā´r</i>- ‘water’, OIr. <i>fír</i> ‘milk’, Lat. <i>ūmor</i> ‘moisture’, Lith. <i>ū́mas</i> ‘quick, fresh, not dry’). IEW 80 f., EIEC 636 f., NIL 715 ff.

151. ‘rain’: *<i>h₂u̯ers</i>- (: Skt. <i>várṣati</i>, Hitt. <i>waršiyezzi</i> ‘drips’, Gk. <i>ouréō</i> ‘I urinate’; nominal forms: Skt. <i>varṣá</i>- ‘rain’, Gk. <i>eérsē</i> ‘dew, drop’, probably Hitt. <i>warša</i>- ‘fog, rain[?]’; probably also Gk. <i>ouranós</i> ‘sky’ < ‘the raining [or urinating?] one’, or related to Ved. <i>várṣman diváḥ</i> ‘the height of the sky’ as ‘the high one’, cf. Janda 2010: 48 ff.). LIV 291 f., IEW 81, NIL 356 f., EIEC 477 f.

152. ‘river’: most languages use derivatives from *<i>sreu̯</i>- ‘flow’ [144] (: Gk. <i>rheũma</i>, <i>rhéos</i>, OIr. <i>srúaim</i>, ORuss. <i>strumenь</i>, Skt. <i>srávas</i>-, OHG <i>stroum</i>, etc.). LIV 588, IEW 1003, NIL 630 ff., EIEC 486. → ‘water, river’ [387].

153. ‘lake’, cf. [154].

154. ‘sea, lake’: *<i>mori</i>- (: Lat. <i>mare</i>, -<i>is</i>, OIr. <i>muir</i>, Goth. <i>marei</i>, Lith. <i>mãre˙</i>, OCS <i>morje</i>). IEW 748, EIEC 503 f.

155. ‘salt’: *<i>sal</i>- (: Lat. <i>sāl</i>, OIr. <i>sál</i>, Skt. <i>sar</i>-<i>ít</i>- ‘river’ [i.e. *<i>sal</i>-<i>h₁i</i>-<i>t</i>- *‘going to the salt’?], Gk. <i>háls</i>, Arm. <i>ał</i>, OCS <i>solь</i>). IEW 878 f., EIEC 498, NIL 586 ff.

156. ‘stone’: *<i>h₂ek̑</i>-<i>me</i>/<i>on</i>- (: Skt. <i>áśman</i>-, Av. <i>asman</i>- ‘stone, sky’, Gk. <i>ákmōn</i> ‘stone’, ‘anvil’, ‘sky’ in <i>ákmōn</i> … <i>ouranós</i> [Hsch.], Lith. <i>akmuõ</i> ‘stone’, <i>ašmuõ</i> ‘sharpness, blade’, OCS <i>kamy</i> ‘stone’; probably Germ. *<i>hemena</i>- ‘sky’, Goth. <i>himins</i>, etc.), → *<i>h₂ek̑</i>- ‘sharp’ [191], cf. also Hitt. <i>ḫēkur</i>- ‘cliff’. IEW 18 ff. EIEC 547 f. → ‘sky’ [162].

157. ‘sand’: Unclear. Gk. <i>ámatʰos</i> (beside <i>ámmos</i>, <i>psámmos</i>, <i>psámatʰos</i>) and Germ. *<i>samada</i>- (: OHG <i>sant</i>, MHG <i>sand</i>/<i>sampt</i>) point to a preform *<i>samH</i>-<i>dʰo</i>- without further connections (Lat. <i>sabulum</i>?, Arm. <i>awaz</i>?). Skt. <i>pām̐sú</i>-, Av. <i>pąsnu</i>-, OCS <i>pěsъkъ</i> ‘sand, dust’, Hitt. <i>paššila</i>- ‘pebble’ from a root *<i>pens</i>-? IEW 145 f., 824. EIEC 499.

158. ‘dust’: cf. [157].

159. ‘earth’: *<i>dʰeg̑ ʰom</i>- (: Hitt. <i>tekan</i>, gen. <i>taknaš</i>, Skt. <i>kṣam</i>-, abl.gen.sg. <i>jmáḥ</i>, loc. sg. <i>jmán</i>, etc., Av. <i>zam</i>-, Toch. A <i>tkaṃ</i>, B <i>keṃ</i>, Gk. <i>kʰtʰṓn</i>, Lat. <i>humus</i>, Lith. <i>žẽmė</i>, OCS <i>zemlja</i>). IEW 414 ff., EIEC 174, NIL 86 ff. → ‘human being’ [38], cf. 1.

160. ‘cloud; be wet’: *<i>nebʰ</i>- (: Gk. <i>sunnépʰei</i> ‘becomes cloudy’, [pf.] <i>ksunnénophen</i> ‘is cloudy’, YAv. vadj. <i>napta</i>- ‘wet’; nominal forms: Skt. <i>nábhas</i> ‘wetness, cloud, mist’, Gk. <i>népʰos</i>, Arm. <i>amp</i>, Lith. <i>debesìs</i> ‘cloud’; Hitt. <i>nepiš</i>-, OIr. <i>nem</i>, OCS <i>nebo</i> ‘sky’, Lat. <i>nebula</i> ‘fog, cloud’, OHG <i>nebul</i> ‘fog’). LIV 448, IEW 315 f., EIEC 110, 477, NIL 499 ff. → ‘rain’ [377]; *<i>mad</i>- ‘be wet, intoxicated’ (: Lat. <i>madēre</i>, -<i>eō</i> ‘be wet’, <i>mador</i> ‘moisture’, Gk. <i>madáō</i>, <i>madarós</i>, Skt. <i>mad</i>- ‘intoxicate o.s.’, OHG <i>muos</i> ‘food’). LIV 421, IEW 694 f., NIL 455 ff., EIEC 638.

161. ‘fog’: cf. [160].

162. ‘sky’: ‘(god of the) (bright) sky’: *<i>di(i̯)ē´u̯s</i> (: Hitt. <i>šiuš</i>, Gk. <i>Zeús</i>, Skt. <i>dyaúḥ</i>, Lat. <i>Iū</i>- in <i>Iūpiter</i>, OIr. <i>día</i> ‘day’, probably Alb. <i>zot</i> ‘god’), IEW 184 ff., EIEC 513, NIL 69 ff. → ‘stone’ [156], → ‘cloud’ [160], → ‘day’ [178], → ‘shine’ [246], → ‘heavenly one, god’ [380].

163. ‘wind’: *<i>h₂u̯eh₁</i>-<i>n̥t</i>- (: Hitt. <i>h̬uwant</i>-, Lat. <i>ventus</i>, Goth. <i>winds</i>, Skt. <i>vāta</i>-, Toch. B <i>yente</i>); *<i>h₂u̯eh₁</i>-<i>i̯u</i>-/-<i>i̯o</i>- (: Skt. <i>vāyú</i>-, Av. <i>vaiiu</i>- ‘air, atmosphere’, Lith. <i>vė́jas</i>). LIV 287, IEW 81–84, EIEC 643 f. → ‘blow’ [98], → ‘breathe’ [99].

164. ‘snow’: ‘stick, snow’: *<i>snei̯gᵘ̯ʰ</i>- (: Gk. <i>neípʰei</i>, Lat. <i>nīvit</i>, OHG <i>snīwit</i>, Lith. <i>sniẽga</i>, YAv. <i>snaēžat</i> ‘will snow’; Skt. <i>sníhyati</i> ‘sticks; becomes wet’, OIr. <i>snigid</i> ‘rains, drips, snows’). LIV 573, IEW 974, NIL 622 ff. EIEC 530 f.

165. ‘ice’: Unclear. Germ. *<i>īsa</i>- ‘ice’ (: OHG OE OFr. <i>īs</i>, ON <i>íss</i>), Av. <i>aēxa</i>- n. ‘frost, ice’, <i>isauu</i>- ‘icy’, probably older meaning in Lith. <i>ýnis</i>, Russ. <i>ínej</i> ‘hoarfrost’. From *<i>h₁ei̯sh₂</i>- ‘impel’ (via ‘spray’, ON <i>eisa</i> ‘spray, foam’)? IEW 301, EIEC 287.

166. ‘smoke’: *<i>dʰuh2mó</i>- (: Gk. <i>tʰūmós</i>, Skt. <i>dhūmá</i>-, Lat. <i>fūmus</i>, Lith. <i>dū́mai</i>, OCS <i>dymъ</i>, OIr. <i>dumacha</i> ‘fog’, OHG <i>toum</i>). From a verbal root *<i>dʰu̯eh2-</i> ‘to smoke’ (: Hitt. <i>tuḫḫuu̯ai-</i>/<i>tuḫḫui-</i> ‘smoke [n.]’ and [denom.] <i>tuḫḫae</i>- ‘cough, sigh’, Gk. <i>tʰúō</i> ‘I sacrifice [burnt offerings]’, Lat. <i>suffīre</i>, -<i>iō</i> ‘fumigate’, CSl. *<i>dujǫ</i>, <i>duti</i> ‘blow’), probably also ‘breathe’ (: Hitt. <i>antuu̯aḫḫaš</i> ‘man’ < *‘having breath inside’, cf. Kloekhorst 2008: 188 f.). LIV 158, IEW 261–267, EIEC 529.

167. ‘fire’: *<i>peh₂u̯er</i>-/<i>u̯en</i>-: (: Hitt. <i>paḫḫur</i>, gen. <i>paḫḫuwenaš</i>, Toch. A <i>pōr</i>, B <i>puwar</i>, Goth. <i>fon</i>, OHG <i>fuir</i>, Gk. <i>pũr</i>, Umbr. <i>pir</i>, Arm. <i>howr</i>, Cz. <i>pýř</i> ‘glowing ashes’). IEW 828, EIEC 202, NIL 540 ff.; *<i>Vgni</i>- (: Skt. <i>agní</i>-, Lat. <i>ignis</i>, Lith. <i>ugnìs</i>, OCS <i>ognь</i>). IEW 293, EIEC 202. Perhaps *<i>H₍₂₎eH₍₂₎ter</i>- (: Av. <i>ātarš</i> ‘fire’, Lat. <i>āter</i> ‘black’, OIr. <i>áith</i> ‘furnace’, Pal. <i>ḫā</i>- ‘be hot’). LIV 257, IEW 69, EIEC 202.

168. ‘ashes’: *<i>h₂eh₁s</i>- (: Hitt. <i>ḫašš</i>-; derivatives: Hitt. <i>ḫāšša</i>- ‘hearth’, Lat. <i>āra</i> ‘altar’), from a verbal root ‘become dry’ (: Lat. <i>arēre</i>, -<i>eō</i> ‘be dry’, Toch. A <i>asatär</i>, B <i>osotär</i> ‘dries up’), cf. [195] LIV 257 f., IEW 68, EIEC 32. → ‘dry’ [195], → ‘star’ [149].

169. ‘burn’: *<i>dʰegᵘ̯ʰ</i>- (: Skt. <i>dáhati</i>, YAv. <i>dažaiti</i>, Lith. <i>degù</i>, <i>dègti</i>, OCS <i>žegǫ</i>, <i>žešti</i>, Alb. <i>djeg</i>, Lat. <i>fovēre</i>, -<i>eō</i> ‘keep warm’). LIV 133 f., IEW 240 f.; *<i>deh₂u̯</i>- (: Skt. <i>dunóti</i> ‘sets on fire’, OHG <i>zuscen</i>* ‘burn’, Gk. <i>daíō</i>, MIr. *<i>dóïd</i>). LIV 104 f., IEW 179 ff.; *<i>h₁eu̯s</i>- ‘burn, scorch’ (: Skt. <i>óṣati</i>, Gk. <i>heúō</i>, Lat. <i>ūrere</i>, -<i>ō</i>). LIV 245, IEW 347 f.; ‘kindle’: *<i>h₂ei̯dʰ</i>- (: Skt. <i>indhé</i>, Gk. <i>aítʰō</i>). LIV 259, IEW 11 f.

170. ‘road, path’: *<i>péntoh₂s</i>, gen. *<i>pn̥th₂és</i> (: Skt. <i>pánthāh</i>,<i>̣</i> gen. <i>patháh</i>,<i>̣</i> Av. <i>paṇtā̊</i>, gen. <i>paθō</i>, Gk. <i>póntos</i> ‘sea’, Lat. <i>pōns</i> ‘bridge’, Arm. <i>hown</i> ‘path’, OCS <i>pǫtь</i>), verbal root ‘find a way’(?) in Goth. <i>finþan</i> ‘find’. LIV 471 f., IEW 808 f., EIEC 202, 487 f.

171. ‘mountain’: *<i>bʰerg̑ʰ</i>- (: Germ. *<i>berga</i>-, OHG <i>berg</i>, ON <i>bjarg</i> etc., Av. *<i>barǝzah</i>-, OCS <i>brěgъ</i> → ‘rise’ [210]). LIV 78 f., IEW 140 f., NIL 30 ff. ‘hill, mountain’: *<i>gᵘ̯erH</i>-(: Skt. <i>girí</i>- f. ‘mountain, hill’, YAv. <i>gairi</i>-, OCS <i>gora</i> f. ‘mountain’, Alb. <i>gur</i> ‘rock, stone’, Lith. <i>girià</i> ‘forest’). IEW 477 f., EIEC 269 f. Probably derived from → ‘heavy’ [31].

172. ‘red’: *<i>h₁rou̯dʰ</i>-<i>o</i>- (: Skt. <i>lohá</i>- ‘reddish’, Lat. (Sabellic) <i>rūfus</i>, OIr. <i>rúad</i>, Welsh <i>rhudd</i>, Goth. <i>rauþs</i>, ON <i>rauðr</i>, OHG <i>rōt</i>, Lith. <i>raũdas</i>, OCS <i>rudъ</i>, Toch. A <i>rote</i> ‘red paint color’; *<i>h₁rudʰ</i>-<i>ro</i>-: Skt. <i>rudhirá</i>-, Gk. <i>eruthrós</i>, Lat. <i>ruber</i>, Umbr. <i>rufru</i> ‘rubros’, OCS <i>rъdrъ</i>, Toch. A <i>rtär</i>, Toch. B <i>ratre</i>). LIV 508 f., IEW 872 ff., NIL 580 ff., EIEC 480 f.

173. ‘green/yellow’: *<i>g̑ ʰˡ̥ʰ</i>3-<i>i</i>-/-<i>o</i>-/-<i>ro</i>-/-<i>(s)u̯o</i>- (: Skt. <i>hári</i>-, Av. <i>zari</i>-, Gk. <i>kʰló(w)os</i> ‘greenish-yellow or light green colour; pallor’, <i>kʰlōrós</i> ‘greenish-yellow, pale green’, Lat. <i>helvus</i> ‘yellowish’, OIr. <i>gel</i> ‘clear’, OHG <i>gelo</i> ‘yellow’, Lith. <i>ge<img src="images/handbook-comparative-historical-indo-european-linguistics-volume-3-img-l-tilde.png" alt="[image-glyph: l with tilde]">[image-glyph: l with tilde] svas</i> ‘yellowish’, <i>že<img src="images/handbook-comparative-historical-indo-european-linguistics-volume-3-img-l-tilde.png" alt="[image-glyph: l with tilde]">[image-glyph: l with tilde] vas</i> ‘green’, OCS <i>zelenъ</i> ‘green’). IEW 429–434, EIEC 246. → ‘gall’ [280].

174. ‘yellow’: cf. [173].

175. ‘white’: *<i>albʰo</i>- (: Gk. <i>alpʰós</i> ‘dull-white leprosy’, Lat. <i>albus</i> ‘white’, Umbr. <i>alfu</i> ‘alba’, Hitt. <i>alpaš</i> ‘cloud’, OHG <i>albiz</i>, ON <i>elptr</i> ‘swan’, OCS <i>lebedь</i> ‘swan’). IEW 30 f.; *<i>h₂erg̑</i>-<i>ro</i>-/-<i>u</i>-/-<i>i</i>- (: Skt. <i>árjuna</i>-, Gk. <i>argós</i>, <i>árgupʰos</i>, Lat. <i>arguere</i>, -<i>ō</i> ‘make clear’, Goth. <i>airkns</i> ‘pure’, Toch. B <i>ārkwi</i>, Hitt. <i>ḫarki</i>- ‘white’). IEW 64 f., NIL 317 f.→‘silver’ [338]; ‘white/brilliant/shining’: *<i>k̑u̯ei̯t</i>- (: Skt. <i>śvetá</i>-, <i>śvitrá</i>-, Av. <i>spaētō</i>, Goth. <i>ƕeits</i>, ON <i>hvítr</i>, OHG <i>hwiz</i> ‘white’, Lith. <i>švitrùs</i> ‘brilliant’, OCS <i>světъ</i> ‘light’). IEW 628 f.; ‘brilliant/shining’: *<i>leu̯kó</i>- (: Skt. <i>rocá</i>-, Gk. <i>leukós</i> ‘shining, white’, OIr. <i>luach</i>, OHG <i>lioht</i> [*<i>leu̯kto</i>-] ‘clear, shiny’, Lith. <i>laũkas</i> ‘pale’, Toch. B <i>lyuke</i>-<i>mo</i> ‘shining’). Verbal root *<i>leu̯k̑</i>- ‘become light’ (: Hitt. <i>lukta</i> ‘becomes light’, Toch. A [pt.] <i>lyokät</i>, Skt. <i>rócate</i> ‘shines’, etc.). LIV 418 f., IEW 687 ff., EIEC 641. → ‘shine’ [246], ‘birch’ [342].

176. ‘black’: *<i>kr̥sno</i>- (: Skt. <i>kr̥sṇạ́</i>-, OPr. <i>kirsna</i>-, OCS <i>črъnъ</i> [Lith. <i>Kirsnà</i> (name of a river, ‘black one’?)]). IEW 583; ‘black, dirty’: *<i>mel(h₂)</i> (: Skt. <i>maliná</i>-, Gk. <i>mélas</i>, <i>mélan</i>- ‘black’, Lat. <i>mulleus</i> ‘purple’?, Welsh <i>melyn</i> ‘yellow’, MHG <i>māl</i> ‘spot’, Lith. <i>mélynas</i> ‘blue’, Latv. <i>melns</i> ‘black’). IEW 720 f., EIEC 69 f.

177. ‘night’: *<i>nokᵘ̯ts</i>, gen. *<i>nekᵘ̯ts</i> (: Skt. <i>nákt</i>-, Lat. <i>nox</i>, Gk. <i>núx</i>, Goth. <i>nahts</i>, Lith. <i>naktìs</i>, OCS <i>noštь</i>, gen. *<i>nekᵘ̯ts</i> in Hitt. <i>nekuz mēḫḫur</i> ‘the time of evening’, OIr. <i>innocht</i> ‘tonight’, Alb. <i>natë</i>, Toch. A <i>nokte</i> ‘at night’). LIV 449, IEW 762 f., NIL 504 ff., EIEC 394.

178. ‘day’: *<i>āmer</i>- (: Gk. <i>ē˜mar</i>, <i>āmérā</i>, Arm. <i>awr</i>). IEW 35; *<i>h₂egʰ</i>- (: Skt. <i>áhaḥ</i>, gen. <i>áhnaḥ</i> OAv. [gen.pl.] <i>asnąm</i>). IEW 7, EIEC 149. → ‘sky’ [162].

179. ‘year’: *<i>h₂et</i>-<i>no</i>- (: Lat. <i>annus</i>, Osc. [dat./loc.] <i>akeneí</i>, Goth. [dat.pl.] <i>aþnam</i>). LIV 273, IEW 69. → ‘go’ [121]; *<i>u̯et</i>-<i>(es)</i>- (: Hitt. <i>witt</i>-, Alb. <i>vit</i>, Gk. [Myc.] <i>we</i>-<i>to</i> /u̯etos/, alph.-Gk. <i>[w]étos</i>, Lat. [→ adj.] <i>vetus</i> ‘old’, Skt. <i>vatsá</i>- ‘calf [*of one year]’, *<i>per</i>-<i>ut</i>-<i>i</i> ‘in the last year’ in Gk. <i>pérusi</i>, Arm. <i>herow</i>, Skt. <i>parút</i>, MHG <i>vert</i>). IEW 1175; *<i>i̯eh₂</i>- <i>r</i>- (: Av. <i>yārǝ</i>, Gk. <i>hṓrā</i> ‘season, time of day, hour’, Goth. <i>jēr</i>, OHG <i>jār</i>, RCS <i>jara</i> ‘spring’). IEW 296 f., EIEC 654. → ‘go’ [121].

256. ‘praise, honour’: *<i>gᵘ̯erH</i>- (: Skt. <i>gr̥ṇā´ti</i>, YAv. -<i>gǝrǝṇte</i>, Lith. <i>giriù</i>, <i>gìrti</i> ‘praise’, OCS <i>žьrjǫ</i>, <i>žrъti</i> ‘sacrifice’). LIV 210 f. IEW 478, EIEC 449 f.

257. ‘worship, sacrifice’: *<i>Hi̯ag̑</i>- (: Skt. <i>yájate</i> ‘sacrifices, worships’, Av. <i>yazaite</i> ‘worships’, Gk. <i>házomai</i> ‘I fear, feel awe, worship’). LIV 224 f., IEW 501, EIEC 650.

258. ‘libate’: *<i>spend</i>- (: Hitt. <i>šipanti</i>, Gk. <i>spéndō</i>, Lat. <i>spondēre</i>, -<i>eō</i>, Toch. B <i>späntetär</i> ‘trusts’). LIV 577 f., IEW 989, EIEC 351.

259. ‘wear’: *<i>u̯es</i>- (: Hitt. <i>wēšta</i>, Skt. <i>váste</i>, OAv. <i>vastē</i>, Gk. <i>hẽmai</i> ‘I wear’, <i>hénnūmi</i> ‘I clothe’, Arm. <i>z</i>-<i>genowm</i> ‘I clothe [myself]’, Toch. B <i>wässāte</i>, A [pl.] <i>wsānte</i> ‘wore, put on’; caus. *<i>u̯os</i>-<i>éi̯e</i>/<i>o</i>- ‘clothe s.b.‘in Hitt. <i>waššiezzi</i>, ved. <i>vāsáyati</i>, OE <i>werian</i>, Alb. <i>vesh</i>). LIV 692 f., IEW 1172 f., EIEC 109 f. → ‘evening, west’ [368], ‘garment, enshrouding’ [369].

260. ‘gird (oneself)’: *<i>i̯eh₃s</i>- (: Gk. <i>zō´nnumi</i>, OLith. [3sg.] <i>juosti</i>, OCS <i>po</i>-<i>jašǫ</i>, -<i>jasati</i>, Alb. <i>n</i> -<i>gjesh</i>; cf. Gk. <i>zō´ma</i>, <i>zōstḗr</i>, <i>zō´nē</i>, OCS <i>po</i>-<i>jasъ</i> ‘girdle’, Lith. <i>júostas</i>, YAv. <i>yāsta</i>-‘girded’). LIV 311, IEW 513, NIL 391 f., EIEC 223 f.

261. ‘build’: *<i>demh₂</i>- (: hLuw. [prt.] <i>tamata</i>, Gk. <i>démō</i>, Goth. <i>gatiman</i> ‘fit’, Toch. B [inf.] <i>tsamtsi</i> ‘create’). LIV 114 ff., IEW 198 f., EIEC 87, Nikolaev 2010.

262. ‘domesticate, tame’: *<i>demh₂</i>- (: Gk. <i>dámnēmi</i>, Skt. <i>damáyati</i>, Lat. <i>domāre</i>, -<i>ō</i>, Goth. <i>ga</i>-<i>tamjan</i>, Hitt. <i>damašzi</i>, OIr. -<i>damna</i>). LIV 116 f., IEW 199 f., EIEC 87.

263. ‘enter; copulate’: *<i>(h₃)i̯ebʰ</i>- (: Skt. <i>yábhati</i> ‘copulates’, Gk. <i>oípʰō</i>, Ukr. <i>jebú</i>, <i>jebáty</i>, Toch. B <i>yopsa</i>, A <i>yowäs</i> ‘entered’). LIV 309, IEW 298, EIEC 507 f.

264. ‘grind, mill’: *<i>h₂leh₁</i>- (: Gk. <i>aléō</i>, Arm. <i>aɫam</i>, khot. <i>ārr</i>-). LIV 277, IEW 28 f.; *<i>melh₂</i>- (: Arm. <i>malem</i>, Lat. <i>molere</i>, -<i>ō</i>, OIr. <i>melid</i>, OCS <i>meljǫ</i>, <i>mlěti</i>, Goth. <i>malan</i>, Lith. <i>malù</i>, <i>málti</i>, Hitt. <i>malli</i>-). LIV 432 f., IEW 716 f., EIEC 247.

265. ‘light’: *<i>h₁le(n)gᵘ̯ʰ</i>-<i>u</i>- (: Skt. <i>raghú</i>-, <i>laghú</i>-, YAv. <i>rǝuuī</i> [f.], Gk. <i>elakʰús</i>, Lat. <i>levis</i> [with regular remodeling to <i>i</i>-stem], OIr. <i>laigiu</i> ‘smaller, worse’, Germ. *<i>lenhta</i>- < *<i>le</i>-<i>n</i>-<i>k⁽ᵘ̯⁾to</i>- [Goth. <i>leihts</i>, ON <i>léttr</i>, OHG <i>līht</i>], Lith. <i>leñgvas</i>, OCS <i>lьgъkъ</i>). LIV 247 f., IEW 660 f., EIEC 353, NIL 243 ff., 450 f., EIEC 353. → ‘lungs’ [281].

266. ‘high’: *<i>bʰr̥g̑ ʰ</i>-<i>u</i>-/-<i>ent</i>- (: Skt. <i>br̥hánt</i>-, Av. <i>bǝrǝz</i>-, Arm. <i>barjr</i>, Hitt. <i>parku</i>-; cf. root noun *<i>bʰr̥g̑ʰ</i>- in Goth. <i>baurgs</i> ‘citadel’; <i>nt</i>-stem also PN OHG <i>Purgunt</i>, OIr. <i>Brigit</i> [*<i>bʰr̥g̑ʰ-n̥t-ī</i>]). LIV 78 f., IEW 140 f., EIEC 269. → ‘mountain’ [171], → ‘rise’ [210].

267. ‘deep’: *<i>dʰeu̯b</i>- (: Lith. <i>dubùs</i>, Goth. <i>diups</i>, Toch. B <i>taupe</i>, A <i>top</i> ‘mine’, MWelsh <i>dwfn</i> ‘deep; world’, OCS <i>dъno</i> ‘ground’, cf. with opposite meaning Toch. B <i>tapre</i>, A <i>tpär</i> ‘high’ [*<i>dʰub</i>-<i>ro</i>-]). IEW 267 f., EIEC 154, NIL 122 ff., EIEC 154.

268. ‘grey’: *<i>as</i>- (: Lat. <i>cānus</i> ‘grey’, esp. in the word for → [341] ‘hare’: OHG <i>haso</i>, ON <i>hǫss</i> [*<i>as</i>-<i>u̯o</i>-], Skt. <i>śaśa</i>- [with assimilation from *<i>śasa</i>], Welsh <i>ceinach</i>, OPr. <i>sasins</i>). IEW 533, EIEC 240, 256 f., NIL 410 f.; *<i>poli</i>-<i>o</i>-/-<i>no</i>-/-<i>to</i>- (: Gk. <i>poliós</i>, Arm. <i>alik‘</i> ‘grey hair, waves’, Skt. <i>palitá</i>- ‘grey, old’, Gk. <i>pelitnós</i>, Lat. <i>pallidus</i> ‘pale’?, MIr. <i>liath</i>, Welsh <i>llwyd</i> ‘grey’ [*<i>pleitos</i>?], OHG <i>falo</i>, ON <i>fǫlr</i> [Germ. *<i>falwaz</i>] ‘pale’, Lith. <i>pa<img src="images/handbook-comparative-historical-indo-european-linguistics-volume-3-img-l-tilde.png" alt="[image-glyph: l with tilde]">[image-glyph: l with tilde] vas</i> ‘pale’, OCS <i>plavъ</i> ‘white’). IEW 804 f., EIEC 240.

269. ‘brown’: *<i>bʰru</i>-<i>(no)</i>-, *<i>bʰer</i>-<i>o</i>- (: Skt. <i>babhrú</i>- ‘brown’, Gk. <i>pʰrũnos</i>/-<i>ē</i> ‘toad’ < ‘brown one’, OHG <i>brūn</i>, Lith. <i>bė́ras</i> ‘brown’, RCS <i>bronъ</i> ‘white’). IEW 136 f., EIEC 85. → ‘beaver’ [347].

270. ‘empty, lacking’: *<i>h₁u̯eh₂-no</i>-/*<i>h₁uh₂-no</i>- (: Lat. <i>vānus</i> ‘empty, idle’, Skt. <i>ūná</i>-‘lacking’, Arm. <i>ownayn</i>, Goth. <i>wans</i> ‘lack’, OHG OE OS <i>wan</i> ‘lacking, empty’), *<i>h₁uh₂- ni</i>- (: Gk. <i>eũnis</i> ‘bereaved of, lacking’), *<i>h₁u̯eh₂-to</i>- (: Lat. <i>vāstus</i>, OIr. <i>fás</i>). LIV 254, IEW 345, 1111, NIL 248 ff., EIEC 179.

271. ‘raw’: *<i>Hōmó</i>- (: Gk. <i>ōmós</i>), *<i>Hō</i>/<i>omo</i>- (: Skt. <i>āmá</i>-, Arm. <i>howm</i>), *<i>Homo</i>- (: OIr. <i>om</i>). IEW 777 f., EIEC 478, NIL 202.

272. ‘fast’: *<i>Hōk̑ú</i>- (: Skt. <i>āśú</i>-, Av. <i>āsu</i>-, Gk. <i>ōkús</i>, Lat. <i>ōcior</i>, <i>ōcius</i> ‘faster’). Perhaps related to → [311] *<i>h₁ek̑u̯</i>-<i>o</i>- ‘horse’ (‘the fast animal’?) or to → [191] *<i>h₂ek̑</i>- ‘sharp’ (cf. de Lamberterie 1990.2: 577, 583). IEW 775, EIEC 194, NIL 200 f.

273. ‘slow’: *<i>gᵘ̯r̥d</i>-<i>u</i>- (: Gk. <i>bradús</i>, Lith. <i>gurdùs</i> ‘slow, dull’). Perhaps related to *<i>gᵘ̯</i>erh₂- ‘heavy’ (cf. de Lamberterie 1990.2: 590 ff.). IEW 476, NIL 195 f.

274. ‘on foot, foot-’: *<i>pedii̯o</i>- (: Skt. <i>pádya</i>- ‘related to the foot’, Lat. <i>acu</i>-<i>pedius</i> ‘swift-footed’, Arm. <i>heti</i> ‘on foot’).

275. ‘broad’: *<i>pl̥th₂-u</i>- (: Skt. <i>pr̥thú</i>-, Av. <i>pǝrǝθu</i>-, Gk. <i>platús</i>, Lith. <i>platùs</i>). LIV 486 f., IEW 833, NIL 564 ff.; probably related to *<i>pleh₂-</i> (: Hitt. <i>palḫi</i>- ‘broad’, Lat. <i>plānus</i> ‘broad, flat’). IEW 805, EIEC 205 f., NIL 562 ff.; *<i>h₁u̯erH</i>- (: Skt. <i>urú</i>-, OAv. <i>vouru</i>-, Gk. <i>eurús</i>, Osc. [f.] <i>uruvú</i>, Toch. A <i>wärts</i>, B <i>wartstse</i> [**<i>h₁u̯r̥H</i>-<i>ti̯o</i>-]). IEW 1165, EIEC 83, NIL 250 ff.

276. ‘old man’: *<i>g̑erh₂-ont</i>- (: Gk. <i>gérōn</i>, -<i>ontos</i>, Oss. <i>zærond</i> ‘old’, Skt. <i>járant</i>- ‘old man’); *<i>g̑erh₂-o</i>- (: Arm. <i>cer</i>, NPers. <i>zar</i>); *<i>g̑erh₂-lo</i>- (: ON <i>karl</i> ‘old man’, OE <i>ceorl</i> ‘freeman of the lowest class’ [NE <i>churl</i>], OHG <i>karal</i> ‘old man’, NHG <i>Kerl</i>); *<i>ǵerh₂-on-</i>(: Toch. B <i>śrān</i>- ‘adult man’). IEW 390 f., EIEC 409 f. → ‘rub, make old’ [252].

277. ‘old woman’: *<i>g̑erh₂-u</i>- (: Gk. <i>graũs</i>, Alb. <i>grua</i> ‘woman’ [or from *<i>gᵘ̯en(h₂)-</i>[36]?]). IEW 391, EIEC 409 f. → ‘old man’ [276].

278. ‘young/young man’: *<i>h₂i̯eu̯</i>- (: OIr. <i>óa</i>, MWelsh <i>ieu</i> ‘younger’; *<i>h₂i̯u</i>-<i>h₃en</i>-: Skt. <i>yúvan</i>-, Av. <i>yauua</i>-, Lat. <i>iuvenis</i>; *<i>h₂i̯ou̯</i>-<i>h₃no</i>-: Lith. <i>jáunas</i>, Latv. <i>jaûns</i>, OCS <i>junъ</i>; *<i>h₂i̯u</i>-<i>h₃n̥</i>-<i>kó</i>-: Goth. <i>juggs</i> [i.e. (ŋg)] [comp. <i>jūhiza</i>], ON <i>ungr</i>, OE <i>geong</i>, OHG <i>jung</i>, OIr. <i>ó[a]c</i>, Welsh <i>ieuanc</i>/<i>ifanc</i> ‘young’, Lat. <i>iuvencus</i> ‘young [cow]’, Skt. <i>yuvaśá</i>-). IEW 510 f., EIEC 655 f. → ‘life’ [108].

279. ‘eyebrow’: *<i>(h₃)bʰruH</i>- (: Skt. <i>bhrū</i>-, Gk. <i>opʰrũs</i>, OIr. <i>brú</i>, Lith. <i>bruvìs</i>, OCS <i>brъvь</i>, Toch. [du.] A <i>pärwām</i>,<i>̣</i> B <i>pärwāne</i>, OE <i>brú[w]a</i>). IEW 172 f., EIEC 188, NIL 41 ff.

280. ‘gall’: *<i>g̑ ʰol-o-</i> (: Gk. <i>kʰólos</i>, <i>kʰolḗ</i>, OHG <i>galla</i>, OCS <i>zlьčь</i>, Av. <i>zāra</i>-, Lat. <i>fel</i>, probably Lith. <i>tulžìs</i> if with metathesis from *<i>g̑ʰol</i>-<i>ti</i>-). IEW 429, EIEC 217. → ‘yellow’ [173].

281. ‘lungs’: *<i>pleu̯-mon</i>- (: Gk. <i>pléumōn</i>, Lat. <i>pulmō</i>, Skt. <i>klóman</i>-), → *<i>pleu̯</i>- ‘float’ [119]. IEW 837 f.; *<i>(h₁)lengᵘ̯ʰ</i>- (: OHG <i>lungūn</i>, NE <i>lights</i>, Russ. <i>le¨gkoje</i>, Arm. <i>lanǰk‘</i> ‘breast’, if from an earlier meaning ‘lungs’). IEW 661, EIEC 359. → ‘light’ [265].

282. ‘arm, forearm’ (: Skt. <i>bāhu</i>́<i>ḥ</i>, Av. <i>bāzāuš</i>, Gr. <i>pẽkʰus</i>, ‘elbow, forearm’, ON <i>bógr</i> ‘arm, shoulder’, OHG <i>buog</i> ‘shoulder, hip’, Toch. АВ <i>poke</i>, В <i>pauke</i> [Arm. <i>bazowk</i> probably an Iranian loanword]). IEW 152, EIEC 26.

283. ‘shoulder’: *<i>Homso</i>- (: Gk. <i>õmos</i>, Skt. <i>ám˙sa</i>-, Lat. <i>umerus</i>, Goth. <i>ams</i>, Toch. A <i>es</i>, B <i>āntse</i>, Arm. <i>ows</i>). IEW 778, EIEC 515 f. Perhaps related to *<i>mē˘ms(o)-</i> ‘meat’ → [63] as *<i>h₁omso</i>- ‘back’ / (vr̥ddhi-derivative) *<i>h₁ōmso</i>- ‘belonging to the back’ (Pinault, ms.).

284. ‘elbow’: *<i>Hol</i>-<i>en</i>- (: Skt. <i>aratní</i>-, Lat. <i>ulna</i>, Gk. <i>ōlénē</i> ‘elbow, forearm’, Goth. <i>aleina</i> ‘cubit’, OHG <i>elina</i>, Alb. <i>le¨re¨</i>, [Geg] <i>lans</i>, Arm. <i>oɫn</i>, gen. <i>oɫin</i> with problematic meaning ‘vertebra, spine, shoulder’). IEW 370, 524, 590, EIEC 176.

285. ‘chin’: *<i>g̑enu</i>- (: Gk. <i>génus</i>, Goth. <i>kinnus</i>*, Skt. <i>hanu</i>-, Av. <i>zanauua</i> [du.] [IIr. forms with secondary anlaut], Lat. <i>gena</i>, air. <i>gi[u]n</i> ‘mouth’, Welsh <i>gen</i>, Toch. A <i>śanwe</i> [du.], Arm. <i>cnawt</i>). IEW 381 (EIEC 107).

286. ‘ship’: *<i>neh₂u</i>- (: Lat. <i>nāvis</i>, Gk. <i>naũs</i>, Skt. <i>naúh</i>̣, OIr. <i>nau</i>, ON <i>nór</i>; probably a derivative from *<i>(s)neh₂-</i> ‘swim’ → [119], but always without the movable <i>#s</i>-, hence probably dissociated from this root already in the proto-language). IEW 755 f., EIEC 74 f., NIL 515 ff.

287. ‘beech tree’: *<i>bʰeh2go</i>- (: Lat. <i>fāgus</i> ‘beech’, Gk. <i>pʰēgós</i> ‘oak’, OHG <i>buocha</i> ‘beech’; also Germ. *<i>bōk[ō]</i>-, OE <i>bōc</i> ‘book’, OHG <i>buocha</i> ‘beech’, etc.). NIL 2, IEW 107 f., EIEC 58 ff.

288. ‘apple, apple tree’: *<i>h₂eb</i>-<i>el</i>- (: Welsh <i>afal</i>, OHG <i>apful</i>, Lith. <i>obelìs</i>, OCz. <i>jablo</i>). IEW 2 f., EIEC 25 f., NIL 262 f.

289. ‘cherry, cherry tree’: *<i>kr̥</i> -<i>no</i>- (: Gk. <i>krános</i>, Lat. <i>cornu</i>-<i>m</i>/-<i>s</i> ‘cornel cherry (tree)’, Gk. <i>kránon</i>, Lith. <i>Kirnis</i> ‘deus cerasorum’). IEW 572 f., EIEC 106.

290. ‘navel’: *<i>h₃nebʰ</i>- (: Gk. <i>ompʰalós</i>, Lat. <i>umbilicus</i>, OHG <i>nabulo</i>, MIr. <i>imbliu</i>, Skt. <i>nābhi</i>-, YAv. <i>nāfa</i>-, Latv. <i>naba</i>). IEW 314 f., EIEC 391, NIL 385 ff.

291. ‘man’: *<i>man</i>-<i>u</i>- (: Skt. <i>mánu</i>-, <i>mánuṣ</i>-, Goth. <i>manna</i>, perhaps OCS <i>mǫžь</i> [*<i>mangi̯a</i>-?]). IEW 700, EIEC 366 f. → [37], [392], [396].

292. ‘son’: *<i>suH</i>-<i>nu</i>-, -<i>i̯u</i>- (: Skt. <i>sūnú</i>-, Av. <i>hunu</i>-, Goth. <i>sunus</i>, OCS <i>synъ</i>, Lith. <i>sūnùs</i>; Gk. <i>huiús</i> and <i>huiós</i>, Toch. A <i>se</i>, B <i>soy</i>, Arm. <i>owstr</i> [*<i>sūi̯u</i>- > *<i>ow</i> /u/, <i>-str</i> from <i>dowstr</i> ‘daughter’]). IEW 913 f., EIEC 533, NIL 686 ff. → ‘give birth’ [227].

293. ‘daughter’: *<i>dʰugh2ter</i>- (: Skt. <i>duhitar</i>-, OAv. <i>dugǝdar</i>-, Arm. <i>dowstr</i>, Gk. <i>tʰugátēr</i>, Osc. <i>futír</i>, Goth. <i>dauhtar</i>, Gaul. <i>duχtir</i>, Lith. <i>duktė˜</i>, Ocs. <i>dъšti</i>, Toch. B <i>tkācer</i>, A <i>ckācar</i>, hLuw. <i>tuwa</i>/<i>itara</i>/<i>i</i>-, Lyc. <i>kbatra</i>-). IEW 277, EIEC 147 f., NIL 126 ff.

294. ‘brother’: *<i>bʰreh2ter</i>- (: Skt. <i>bhrā´tar</i>-, Av. <i>brātar</i>-, Lat. <i>frāter</i>, Gk. <i>pʰrḗtēr</i> ‘member of a brotherhood’, Goth. <i>broþar</i>, Arm. <i>eɫbayr</i>, OIr. <i>bráth[a]ir</i>, OCS <i>brat[r]ъ</i>, Lith. <i>broterė˜lis</i>, Toch. A <i>pracar</i>, B <i>procer</i>). IEW 163 f., EIEC 84, NIL 38 ff. Perhaps derived from *<i>bʰer</i>- ‘to bear’ → [223], cf. Pinault (2007).

295. ‘grandson’: *<i>nepot</i>- (: Skt. <i>nápāt</i>-, YAv. <i>napāt</i>-, Gk. <i>népodes</i>, Lat. <i>nepōs</i>, -<i>ōtis</i>, OIr. <i>nia</i> ‘nephew, sister’s son’, OLith. <i>nepuotìs</i> ‘grandson, nephew’, OHG <i>nevo</i> ‘grandson, sister’s son’), fem. *<i>nept</i>-<i>ih₂-</i> (: Skt. <i>naptī́</i>-, YAv. <i>napti</i>-, Lat. <i>neptis</i>, OIr. <i>necht</i>, OLith. <i>neptė</i>, OHG <i>nift</i>). Lat. <i>nepōs</i> means ‘grandson’ in the older language, from the 2<sup>nd</sup> c. CE onwards also ‘nephew’. Similarly, OHG <i>nevo</i> and <i>nift</i> meant ‘grandson/-daughter’ originally, cf. Hettrich (1985). IEW 764, EIEC 239 f., NIL 520 ff.

296. ‘husband’s brother’: *<i>deh₂iu̯er</i>- (: Ved. <i>devár</i>-, Gk. <i>dāḗr</i>, Lat. <i>lēvir</i>, Arm. <i>taygr</i>, OE <i>tācor</i>, Lith. <i>dieverìs</i>, RCS <i>děverъ</i>). IEW 179, EIEC 84, NIL 58 ff.

297. ‘husband’s brother’s wife, sister-in-law’: *<i>Hi̯enh₂ter</i>- (: Skt. <i>yātar</i>-, Gk. [Hom. pl.] <i>einatéres</i>, Arm. <i>nēr</i>, Lat. <i>ianitrīcēs</i>, Lith. <i>jentė</i>, OCS <i>jętry</i>). IEW 505 f., EIEC 522, NIL 204 ff., Kölligan (2012: 142–144).

298. ‘house’: *<i>dom(h₂)</i>-<i>s</i>, gen. *<i>dem(h₂)</i>-<i>s</i> (: Ved. <i>pátir dán</i> ‘lord of the house’, <i>dam</i>-, Av. <i>dam</i>-, Lat. <i>domī</i> ‘at home’, <i>domus</i> ‘house, home’, Gk. <i>dõ</i>, <i>dõma</i>, <i>dómos</i> ‘layer, house, room’, Arm. <i>town</i>, Lith. <i>nãmas</i> [with assimilation <i>d</i> - <i>m</i> > <i>n</i> - <i>m</i>], OCS <i>domъ</i> [<i>u</i>-st.]). LIV 114 ff., IEW 198 f., EIEC 281 f., Nikolaev (2010).

299. ‘settlement’: *<i>u̯ei̯k̑</i>- (: Skt. <i>viś</i>- ‘settlement, house, clan’, Av. <i>vīs</i>- ‘house, village, clan’, Lat. <i>vīcus</i> ‘village’, Gk. <i>[w]oĩkos</i>, <i>[w]oikía</i> ‘house’, Goth. <i>weihs</i> ‘village’, Lith. <i>viẽšpat[i]s</i> ‘lord, master’, OPr. <i>waispattin</i> ‘lady, housewife’, OCS <i>vьsъ</i> ‘village’). LIV 669 f., IEW 1129, 1131, EIEC 622.

300. ‘master of the house’: *<i>dems poti</i>- (: Av. <i>də̄ṇg paiti</i>-, Gk. <i>despótēs</i>, Ved. <i>pátir dán</i> ~ <i>dampati</i>-, with different first element *<i>u̯ei̯k̑</i>- Lith. <i>viẽšpat(i)s</i> → ‘settlement’ [299]).

301. ‘stranger’: *<i>gʰosti</i>- (: Lat. <i>hostis</i> ‘enemy, stranger’, Goth. <i>gasts</i>, OCS <i>gostь</i> ‘guest’; usually analyzed as belonging to a root *<i>g⁽ᵘ̯⁾ʰes</i>- ‘eat’, Skt. <i>ghas</i>-, Av. <i>has</i>-). IEW 453, EIEC 249, NIL 173.

302. ‘grain’: *<i>g̑r̥h₂no</i>- (: Lat. <i>grānum</i>, OIr. <i>grán</i>, Lith. <i>žìrnis</i> ‘pea’, OCS <i>zrъno</i>, Goth. <i>kaurn</i>). IEW 391, EIEC 236 f. → ‘rub, make old’ [252].

303. ‘spelt, corn, barley’: *<i>i̯eu̯o</i>- (: Gk. <i>zeiaí</i> ‘emmer’, Skt. <i>yáva</i>- ‘corn; barley’, Lith. <i>jãvas</i> ‘corn’, Hitt. <i>ewa</i>- ‘corn’). IEW 512, EIEC 236, NIL 407 ff.

304. ‘wheat’: *<i>puHro</i>- (: Gk. <i>pūrós</i>, Lith. <i>pūraĩ</i>, OCS <i>pyro</i> ‘spelt’, OE <i>fyrs</i> ‘furze’). IEW 850, EIEC 639 f.

305. ‘barley’: *<i>bʰar</i>-<i>es</i>- (: Lat. <i>far</i>, gen. <i>farris</i> ‘spelt; flour’, ON <i>barr</i> ‘barley’, OCS <i>brašьno</i> ‘food’). IEW 111, EIEC 51 f.

306. ‘rye’: *<i>u̯rugʰ</i>-<i>i̯o</i>- (: OHG <i>roggo</i>, OE <i>ryge</i> [> NE <i>rye</i>], Lith. <i>rugỹs</i>, pl. <i>rugiaĩ</i>, ORuss. <i>rъžь</i>, perhaps Thrac. <i>bríza</i>). IEW 1183, EIEC 491 f.

307. ‘cut, pluck, reap’: *<i>(s)kerp</i>- (: Lat. <i>carpere</i>, -<i>ō</i> ‘pluck’, Lith. <i>kerpù</i>, <i>kir˜pti</i> ‘cut’, OCS <i>črěpljǫ</i>, <i>črъpati</i> ‘scoop’). LIV 559, IEW 944 f., EIEC 258. → ‘harvest’ [308].

308. ‘harvest’: *<i>korpisto</i>- (: Germ. *<i>harbista</i>-, OHG <i>herbist</i>, OE <i>hærvest</i>). LIV 559, IEW 944 f., EIEC 258. → ‘cut, pluck, reap’ [307], → ‘harvest’ [333].

309. ‘sickle’: *<i>kr̥p</i>-<i>o</i>- (: MIr. <i>corrán</i>, Russ. <i>čerp</i>, Gk. <i>krōpíon</i>, cf. also Skt. <i>kr̥pānạ</i> - ‘sword’). LIV 559, IEW 944 f. → ‘cut, pluck, reap’ [307].

310. ‘plough’: *<i>h₂erh₃-tro</i>- (: Lat. <i>arātrum</i>, Gk. <i>árotron</i>, Arm. <i>arawr</i>, Lith. <i>árklas</i>). IEW 62, EIEC 434 f.

311. ‘horse’: *<i>h₁ek̑u̯os</i> (: Skt. <i>áśva</i>-, Lat. <i>equus</i>, gr. <i>híppos</i> [Myc. <i>i</i>-<i>qo</i>], OIr. <i>ech</i>, OE <i>eoh</i>, Toch. B <i>yakwe</i>, A <i>yuk</i>, hLuv. <i>á-zú-[wa</i>/<i>i]-</i>, Arm. <i>ēš</i> ‘donkey’), prob. related to adj. → ‘fast, swift’ [272] (*<i>h₁ok̑-u-</i> ‘swiftness’ → *<i>h₁ek̑-u̯-o-</i> ‘having swiftness’ as analyzed by J. Schindler, cf. Balles 1997:221 fn. 8). IEW 301 f., EIEC 273 f., NIL 230 ff., Hackstein (2012).

312. ‘cow’: *<i>gᵘ̯ō´u̯s</i>, gen. *<i>gᵘ̯óu̯s</i> (: Skt. <i>gáuḥ</i>, gen. <i>góḥ</i>, Av. <i>gāuš</i>, gen. <i>gə̄uš</i>, Arm. <i>kov</i>, Gk. <i>boũs</i>, Lat. <i>bōs</i>, <i>bovis</i> [Osc.-Umbr. loanword instead of expected *<i>vōs</i>], OIr. <i>bó</i>, OHG <i>chuo</i>, Toch. 313. ‘bull, ox’: *<i>h₂uks</i>-<i>en</i>- (: Skt. <i>ukṣán</i>-, Av. <i>uxšan</i>-, Goth. <i>auhsa</i>*, OIr. <i>oss</i>, Toch. B <i>okso</i>, A [pl.] <i>opsi</i>). IEW 1118, EIEC 135, NIL 368. Perhaps from *<i>h₂u̯eks</i>- ‘grow, become strong’ → [209].

314. ‘sheep’: *<i>h₂ou̯i</i>- (: Skt. <i>avi</i>-, Luw. <i>ḫawiš</i>, Gk. <i>ó[w]is</i>, Lat. <i>ovis</i>, Toch. IEW 784, EIEC 510 ff., NIL 335 ff.

315. ‘lamb’: *<i>h₂egᵘ̯⁽ʰ⁾no</i>- (: Lat. <i>agnus</i>, Gk. <i>amnós</i>, OIr. <i>úan</i>, OE <i>[</i>*<i>ge</i>-<i>]ēanian</i> [> NE <i>yean</i>], OCS <i>[j]agnę</i>). IEW 9.

316. ‘goat’: *<i>h₂ei̯g̑</i>- (: Gk. <i>áiks</i>, gen. <i>aigós</i>, Arm. <i>ayc</i>, cf. Av. <i>izaēna</i>- ‘leathern’). IEW 13; *<i>gʰai̯do</i>- (: Lat. <i>haedus</i> m., Goth. <i>gaits</i>). 318. ‘farrow, pig’: *<i>pork̑o</i>- (: Lat. <i>porcus</i>, Lith. <i>paršas</i>, CSl. <i>prasę</i>, MIr. <i>orc</i>, OHG <i>far[a]h</i>, OE <i>fearh</i>, Khot. <i>pāsa</i>). IEW 820 f., EIEC 425 ff. → ‘furrow’ [319], → ‘speckled’ [320].

319. ‘furrow’: *<i>perk̑</i>- (: Lat. <i>porca</i>, Welsh <i>rhych</i>, OHG <i>furuh</i>, OE <i>furh</i>, Lith. <i>pra</i>-<i>par˜šas</i> ‘ditch’). 320. ‘speckled’: *<i>perk̑</i> - (: Gk. <i>perknós</i> ‘dark’, Skt. <i>pŕ̥śnị</i>- ‘speckled, coloured’; Lat. <i>porcus</i> [a type of fish], MIr. <i>orc</i> ‘salmon’). IEW 820 f., EIEC 537. → ‘farrow, pig’ [318].

322. ‘broth, soup’: *<i>i̯uHs</i> (: Skt. <i>yū´ḥ</i>, <i>yūṣán-</i>, Lat. <i>iūs</i>, gen. <i>iūris</i>, ORuss. <i>ucha</i>, Lith. <i>jū´šė</i>, probably Gk. <i>zū´mē</i> ‘leaven’, Germ. *<i>justa</i>- in ON <i>ostr</i> ‘cheese’). IEW 507, EIEC 84.

323. ‘put on, wear’: *<i>h₂eu̯H</i>- (: Lat. <i>ind</i>-/<i>ex</i>-<i>uere</i>, -<i>ō</i> ‘put on/off’, Arm. <i>aganim</i> ‘I wear’, Lith. <i>aunù</i>, <i>aũti</i>, OCS <i>obujǫ</i>, -<i>uti</i> ‘put on shoes’; cf. also Av. <i>aoθra</i>- ‘shoe’). LIV 275, IEW 346, EIEC 109.

324. ‘axle; axis’: *<i>h₂ek̑s</i>- (:‘axis’: Lat. <i>axis</i>, Lith. <i>ašìs</i>, OCS <i>osь</i>, Gk. <i>áksōn</i>, Ved. <i>ákṣa</i>-, OHG OS <i>ahsa</i>, OE <i>eax</i>; ‘axle’: Lat. <i>āla</i> ‘axle, wing’, OHG OE <i>ahsla</i>, OE <i>eaxel</i>). IEW 6, EIEC 39 f., NIL 259 ff.

325. ‘testicle’: *<i>h₁org̑ʰi</i>- (: Gk. <i>órkʰis</i>, Arm. [pl.] <i>orjik‘</i>, Alb. <i>herdhe</i>, MIr. <i>uirgge</i>, Av. [du.] <i>ǝrǝzi</i>) → *<i>h₁erg̑ʰ</i>- [211]; cf. also the adj. 326. ‘penis’: *<i>pes</i>- (: Skt. <i>pásas</i>-, Gk. <i>péos</i>, Lat. <i>pēnis</i>, OHG <i>fasel</i>, OE <i>fæsl</i>). IEW 824, EIEC 507 f.

327. ‘wheel’: *<i>kᵘ̯e</i>-<i>kᵘ̯</i>lh₁-<i>o</i>- (: Skt. <i>cakrá</i>-, Av. <i>čaxra</i>-, Gk. <i>kúklos</i> ‘circle’, pl. <i>kúkloi</i>/-<i>a</i> ‘wheels’, OE <i>hwēol</i> [> NE <i>wheel</i>], ‘chariot’: Toch. A <i>kukäl</i>, B <i>kokale</i>). LIV 386, IEW 639 f., EIEC 640 f. → ‘turn’ [126].

328. ‘morning’: *<i>h₂ei̯</i>-<i>r</i>/<i>n</i>- (: Av. <i>aiiarǝ</i> ‘day’ [replacing *<i>h₂egʰ</i>-], Gk. <i>áriston</i> ‘breakfast’ < *<i>ai̯eri</i>-<i>[h₁]d</i>-<i>tom</i> cf. [93], adv. <i>ẽri</i> ‘in the morning’, Goth. <i>air</i> ‘early’). IEW 12, EIEC 173, NIL 258 f.

329. ‘darkness’: *<i>(h₁)regᵘ̯os</i> (: Gk. <i>érebos</i> ‘underworld; darkness’, Skt. <i>rájas</i>- ‘[dark] space’, Goth. <i>riqis</i> ‘darkness’, ON <i>røkkr</i> ‘twilight’, Arm. <i>erek</i> ‘evening’). IEW 857, EIEC 147, NIL 573 f.

330. ‘dawn’: *<i>h₂éu̯sōs</i>, gen. *<i>h₂us</i>-<i>s</i>-<i>és</i> (: Skt. <i>uṣás</i>-, Av. <i>ušah</i>-, Gk. [Lesb.] <i>aúōs</i>, [Att.] <i>héōs</i>, Lat. <i>aurōra</i>, Lith. <i>aušrà</i>). LIV 292, IEW 86 f., EIEC 148 f.

340. ‘bear’: *<i>h₂r̥tk̑o</i>- (: Hitt. <i>ḫartagga</i>-, Lat. <i>ursus</i>, Skt. <i>ŕ̥kṣa</i>-, Gk. <i>árktos</i>, Arm. <i>arǰ</i>, OIr. <i>art</i>, Alb. <i>arí</i>). IEW 875, EIEC 55 f., NIL 343.

342. *<i>bʰ</i>(<i>e</i>)<i>rHg̑</i>- ‘birch’ (: OHG <i>birka</i>, ON <i>bjǫrk</i>, OE <i>beorc</i>, Skt. <i>bhūrjá</i>-, Russ. <i>berëza</i>, Lith. <i>béržas</i>, probably Lat. <i>fraxinus</i> ‘ash tree’; probably derived from a root ‘to shine; white’, *<i>bʰreHg̑</i>-, cf. 350. ‘sparrow’: *<i>sper</i>-<i>u̯o(n)</i>- (: Goth. <i>sparwa</i>, Gk. <i>sparásion</i>, prob. <i>psā´r</i> ‘starling’, Toch. A <i>spār</i> [bird]). IEW 991, EIEC 534.

352. ‘starling’: *<i>ster</i>- (: OHG <i>stara</i>, Lat. <i>sturnus</i>, probably OPr. *<i>starnite</i> ‘mew’ [ms. <i>stamite</i>], Russ. <i>strenátka</i> ‘yellowhammer’). IEW 1036, EIEC 534.

355. ‘wasp’: *<i>u̯opseh₂</i>- or *<i>u̯obʰ</i>seh₂- (: OHG <i>wefs[a]</i>, OE <i>wæsp</i>, <i>wæps</i>, <i>wæfs</i>, Lat. <i>vespa</i>, RCS <i>osa</i>, Lith. <i>vapsà</i>, OIr. <i>foich</i>; MP <i>vaβz</i> ‘wasp’), perhaps derived from → *<i>u̯ebʰ</i>- ‘weave’ [251]. IEW 1179, EIEC 636.

356. ‘hornet’: *<i>r̥Hs</i>-<i>ro</i>- (: OHG <i>hornuz</i>/-<i>iz</i>, OE <i>hyrnet[u]</i>, Lat. <i>crābro</i>, Lith. <i>šìršė</i>, RCL <i>strъšerь</i>/<i>srъšerь</i>). IEW 576, EIEC 273. → ‘horn’ [68].

357. ‘fly’ (n.): *<i>mus</i>- (: Gk. <i>muĩa</i>, Lat. <i>musca</i>, Lith. <i>mùsė</i>, OCS <i>muxa</i>, Arm. <i>mown</i>, <i>mnoy</i> ‘gnat’). IEW 752, EIEC 207 f.

358. ‘bee’: *<i>bʰei̯</i>- (: *<i>bini</i>- in OHG <i>bīna</i>, <i>bini</i>, *<i>biōn</i>- in ON <i>bý</i>, OE <i>bēo</i>, OHG <i>bīa</i>, *<i>bʰikelā</i>- in OCS <i>bьčela</i>; Lith. <i>bìtė</i>; OIr. <i>bech</i> [*<i>bʰekos</i>]). IEW 116, EIEC 57 f.

359. ‘honey’: *<i>melit</i>- (: Gk. <i>méli</i>, gen. <i>mélitos</i>, Hitt. <i>milit</i>, Lat. <i>mel</i>, <i>mellis</i>, Arm. <i>mełr</i>, Alb. <i>mjal</i>, OIr. <i>mil</i>, Goth. <i>miliþ</i>, OE <i>mildēaw</i> ‘nectar’, OHG <i>militou</i>). IEW 723 f., EIEC 271.

360. ‘vulva’: *<i>gᵘ̯ʰei̯bʰ</i>- (: Germ. *<i>weiba</i>- ‘woman, wife’, OHG <i>wīb</i>, OE <i>wīf</i> etc., Toch. A <i>kip</i>, B <i>kwipe</i> ‘pudenda muliebra’). IEW 1131 (*<i>u̯ei̯b</i>/<i>p</i>-), EIEC 507 f., Strunk (1989).

361. ‘ruling; ruler’: *<i>h₃rēg̑</i>- (: Skt. <i>rā´j</i>-, Lat. <i>rēx</i>, OIr. <i>rí</i>, Gaul. PN -<i>rix</i>, Goth. <i>reiks</i> ‘ruler’ is a Celtic loan). IEW 855 f., EIEC 329 f. → ‘straight’ [159], → ‘make straight’ [253].

362. ‘believe, trust’: *<i>red dʰ</i>eh₁- ‘put the heart’ (: Skt. <i>śrad dhā</i>-, Av. <i>zrazdā</i>- ‘trusting, believing’, Lat. <i>crēdere</i>, -<i>ō</i>, OIr. <i>cretim</i>). IEW 580, EIEC 61. → ‘heart’ [90], → ‘place, put’ [224].

363. ‘retreat, shy away from, feel awe’: *<i>ti̯egᵘ̯</i>- (: Skt. <i>tyaj</i>-, Gk. <i>sébomai</i>, caus. <i>sobéō</i> ‘I drive away’) LIV 643, IEW 1086, EIEC 650.

364. ‘attend to, worship’: *<i>sep</i>- (: Skt. <i>sápati</i>, OAv. <i>haptī</i>, Gk. <i>hépō</i>). LIV 534, IEW 909, EIEC 450.

365. ‘holy, set apart’: *<i>sak</i>- (: Lat. <i>sacer</i> ‘holy; damned’, i.e. in both cases outside human society, <i>sanctus</i> ‘untouchable, holy’, Hitt. <i>šaklai</i>- ‘custom, rite’, cf. Benveniste 1969.2: 179 ff.), IEW 878, EIEC 493 f.

366. ‘whole, holy’: *<i>kai̯lo</i>- (: Goth. <i>hails</i> ‘in good health’, Germ. *<i>hailaga</i>-: *<i>haila</i>- > NE <i>holy</i>: <i>whole</i>, NHG <i>heilig</i>: <i>heil</i>, OCS <i>cělъ</i> ‘whole, healthy’, <i>cěljǫ</i> ‘I heal’, OPr. <i>kails</i> ‘wholesome, unharmed’). IEW 520, EIEC 262.

367. ‘holy, having supernatural power’: *<i>u̯ento</i>- (: Av. <i>spǝnta</i>-, OCS <i>svęntъ</i>, Lith. <i>šveñtas</i>), probably related to Av. <i>sūra</i>- ‘strong’, Skt. <i>śū́ra</i>- ‘id.’ from <i>śvā</i> ‘swell’, Gk. <i>kuéō</i> ‘I am pregnant’, <i>kũma</i> ‘wave’, <i>kū́rios</i> ‘lord, master’, etc.), cf. Benveniste (1969.2: 182 f.). IEW 630 f., EIEC 493 f.

368. ‘evening, west’: *<i>u̯espero</i>- (: Lat. <i>uesper</i>, Gk. <i>hésperos</i>), perhaps derived from a locative *<i>u̯esper</i> ‘at the (time of) enshrouding’, cf. Katz (2000). IEW 1173 f., EIEC 184. → ‘wear’ [259], → ‘garment, enshrouding’ [369].

369. ‘garment, enshrouding’: *<i>u̯esp</i>- (: Hitt. <i>wašpa</i>- ‘garment’, Lat. <i>uespillō</i> ‘undertaker’ < *‘enshrouder’, probably Gk. <i>ósprion</i> ‘pulse’ [i.e. ‘beans’]), probably related to *<i>u̯es</i>-‘clothe’. IEW −, EIEC 109 f. → ‘wear’ [259], → ‘evening, west’ [368].

370. ‘boy, young man’: *<i>magʰu</i>- (: Goth. <i>magus</i>, f. <i>mawi</i> ‘young girl’, OIr. <i>maug</i> ‘slave’, Alb. <i>makth</i> ‘young hare’, Av. <i>maγava</i>- ‘bachelor’). IEW 696, EIEC 655 f.

371. ‘young (wo)man’: *<i>meri̯o</i>- (: Skt. <i>márya</i>-, Av. <i>mairiia</i>- ‘villain’, Gk. m./f. <i>meĩraks</i>, perhaps Welsh <i>morwyn</i> ‘girl’, <i>merch</i> ‘daughter’, Lith. <i>martì</i>, <i>mergà</i>). IEW 738, EIEC 655 f.

372. ‘womb’: *<i>gᵘ̯elbʰu</i>- (: Skt. <i>gárbha</i>-, Av. <i>garǝβa</i>-, <i>gǝrǝbuš</i> ‘young, child’, Gk. <i>delpʰús</i>, from which <i>delpʰī́s</i>, gen. <i>delpʰĩnos</i> ‘dolphin’ [‘the fish with a womb’], cf. also Gk. <i>a</i>-<i>delpʰ(e)ós</i>, Skt. <i>sá</i>-<i>garbhya</i>- ‘brother’, both [virtually] deriving from *<i>sm̥</i> -<i>gᵘ̯elbʰ</i>- ‘stemming from the same womb’). IEW 473, EIEC 615.

373. ‘grandfather’: *<i>Heu̯Ho</i>- (: Hitt. <i>ḫuḫḫa</i>-, Arm. <i>haw</i>, Lat. <i>avus</i>, ON <i>afi</i>; derivative in Goth. <i>awō</i> ‘grandmother’). IEW 89, EIEC 237 f.

374. ‘(maternal) uncle’: *<i>Heu̯on</i>- (with further suffixes: Lat. <i>avunculus</i>, Welsh <i>ewythr</i>). IEW 89, EIEC 609.

375. ‘goose’: *<i>g̑ʰans</i>- (: Skt. <i>haṃsá</i>-, Gk. <i>kʰḗn</i>, Lat. <i>ānser</i>, OHG <i>gans</i>, Lith. <i>žąsìs</i>, OIr. <i>géis</i> ‘swan’, usually connected with *<i>g̑ʰan</i>- ‘yawn’, Gk. <i>kʰaínō</i>/<i>kʰáskō</i>, Lat. <i>hiāre</i>, -<i>ō</i>, Lith. <i>žióju</i>, -<i>óti</i>, OCS <i>zějǫ</i>, Toch. B <i>kāy</i>- ‘open’). IEW 412, EIEC 236.

376. ‘shed, rain’: *<i>sh₂eu̯</i>- (: Hitt. <i>šuḫḫai</i> ‘sheds, sprinkles’, Gk. <i>hū́ei</i>, Toch. B <i>suwaṃ</i> ‘rains’, cf. nominal formations such as Gk. <i>hūetós</i> ‘[strong] rain’, Alb. <i>shi</i>, Toch. A <i>swase</i>, B <i>swese</i> ‘rain’). LIV 545, IEW 912, EIEC 477 f. → ‘rain’ [377].

377. ‘rain’: *<i>Hembʰ</i>- (: Gk. <i>ómbros</i>, Lat. <i>imber</i>, Skt. <i>ámbhas</i>- ‘water, flood’, <i>abhrá</i>-‘cloud’, YAv. <i>aβra</i>- ‘rain, cloud’). IEW 316, cf. Schrijver (1991: 64), EIEC 477 f. → ‘cloud’ [160].

378. ‘standing water, swamp’: *<i>sel</i>-<i>es</i>- (: Gk. <i>hélos</i>, Skt. <i>sáras</i>-). IEW 901, EIEC 370.

379. ‘rib’: *<i>perk̑</i>- (: Skt. <i>párśu</i>-, Av. <i>parǝsu</i>-/<i>pǝrǝsu</i>-, OCS <i>prъsi</i> (pl.) ‘breasts’, Lith. (žem.) <i>pìršys</i> ‘horse-breast’). IEW 820, EIEC 81.

380. ‘heavenly one, god’: *<i>dei̯u̯ós</i> (: Lat. <i>deus</i>, adj. <i>dīvus</i>, Lith. <i>diẽvas</i>, OHG <i>Ziu</i>, OE <i>Tīw</i>, <i>Tī[g]</i>, ON <i>Týr</i> [: pl. <i>tívar</i> ‘gods’], Hitt. ᵈ<i>Šiu</i>, Luw. <i>Tiwat</i>-, Pal. <i>Tiyaz</i> ‘sun-god’). IEW 184 ff., 416 f., EIEC 513, NIL 69 ff. → ‘sky’ [162], → ‘shine’ [246].

381. ‘beard’: *<i>smek̑ru</i>- (: Skt. <i>śmáśru</i>-, Arm. <i>mawrowk‘</i>, Lith. <i>smãkras</i>, <i>smakrà</i> ‘chin’, Hitt. <i>zama[n]kur</i>-). IEW 968; *<i>bʰar(s)dʰo</i>-/<i>eh₂</i>- (: OHG <i>bart</i>, Lat. <i>barba</i>, OCS <i>brada</i>, Lith. <i>barzdà</i>). NIL 4, IEW 110, EIEC 251.

<!-- source-file: content/14_chapter08_15.xhtml -->

382. ‘corn, seed’: *<i>dʰoh₁</i>neh₂- (: Skt. <i>dhānā´</i>- ‘roasted corn, seeds’, Lith. <i>dúona</i> ‘bread’, Toch. A <i>tāṃ</i>‘corn, seed’, B <i>tāno</i>). IEW 242, EIEC 237, NIL 125. → ‘place, put’ [224].

383. ‘door, wing of a door’: *<i>dʰu̯or</i>- (: Hitt. [adv.] <i>andurza</i> ‘inside’, Skt. <i>dvā´r</i>-, Av. <i>duuar</i>-, Arm. <i>dowr̄n</i>, Gk. <i>tʰúra</i>, Lat. <i>foris</i>, OE <i>duru</i>, OLith. <i>dùres</i>, Lith. <i>dùrys</i>, OCS <i>dvьrь</i>). IEW 278 ff., EIEC 168 f., NIL 130 ff.

384. ‘son-in-law’: *<i>g̑emH</i>-<i>(t)er</i>-/-<i>ro</i>-/-<i>to</i>- (: Lat. <i>gener</i>, Skt. <i>jā´mātar</i>-, Gk. <i>gambrós</i>, Alb. <i>dhëndërr</i>, Lith. <i>žéntas</i>, OCS <i>zętь</i>); cf. YAv. <i>zǝmanā</i>- ‘payment’. IEW 369 f., NIL 136, Bailey (1979: 345), Tremblay (2003: 156), EIEC 533.

385. ‘buttocks’: *<i>Horso</i>- (: Hitt. <i>arra</i>-, Arm. <i>or̄</i>, Gk. <i>órros</i>, OHG <i>ars</i>, MIr. <i>err</i>), perhaps related to *<i>h₁er</i>- [213] or *<i>h₃er</i>- [214]. IEW 340, EIEC 88, NIL 246 ff.

386. ‘door post’: *<i>h₂ent(H)</i>- (: Skt. <i>ā´tā</i>-, YAv. [loc.pl.] <i>aθāhuua</i> ‘house’, Lat. <i>antae</i>, Arm. <i>dr</i>-<i>and</i> ‘threshold’, ON <i>ǫnd</i> ‘aisle, vestibule’). IEW 42, EIEC 168, NIL 306 f.

387. ‘water, river’: *<i>h₂ep</i>- (: Hitt. <i>ḫāppa</i> ‘to the river’, Skt. <i>áp</i>-, OAv. <i>ap</i>-, OPr. <i>ape</i>, Lith. <i>ùpė</i>, Toch. AB <i>āp</i>-, Lat. <i>amnis</i> ‘river’, OIr. <i>ab</i>, <i>o</i>/<i>aub</i> ‘river’, MIr. <i>abann</i>, MWelsh <i>afon</i> ‘id.’). IEW 1, 51 f., 1149, EIEC 486, 636, NIL 311 ff. → ‘water’ [150].

388. ‘middle’: *<i>medʰi̯o</i>- (: Skt. <i>mádhya</i>-, OAv. <i>maidiia</i>-, Gk. <i>mésos</i>, Lat. <i>medius</i>, OIr. <i>mid</i>°, Goth. <i>midjis</i>, Lith. <i>mẽdžias</i> ‘tree, wood’, OCS <i>mežda</i> ‘border, alley’, Arm. <i>mēǰ</i>). IEW 706 f., EIEC 380.

389. ‘mead’: *<i>medʰu</i>- (: cLuv. <i>maddu</i>- ‘wine’, Skt. <i>mádhu</i>- ‘sweet drink, honey’, YAv. <i>maδu</i>- ‘wine’, Gk. <i>métʰu</i> ‘wine’, OE <i>medu</i> ‘mead’, Lith. <i>medùs</i> ‘honey’, OCS <i>medъ</i> ‘honey, mead’, Toch. B <i>mit</i> ‘honey’). IEW 707, EIEC 271, NIL 467 ff.

390. ‘wine’: *<i>u̯oi̯no</i>- (: Lat. <i>vīnum</i>, Gk. <i>[w]oínos</i>, Hitt. <i>wii̯ana</i>-, Arm. <i>gini</i>, Alb. <i>vérë</i>). IEW −, EIEC 644 ff.

391. ‘spruce, pine’: *<i>peu̯k̑</i>- (: Gk. <i>peúkē</i> ‘spruce, pine’, Lith. <i>pušìs</i> ‘pine’, OIr. <i>ochtach</i> ‘spruce’, OHG <i>fiohta</i> ‘spruce’). IEW 828, EIEC 428, NIL 553 f.

392. ‘male’: *(<i>h₁</i>)<i>r̥sen</i>- (: YAv. <i>aršan</i>- ‘man, male’, Arm. <i>ar̄n</i> ‘ram’, Gk. <i>érsēn</i>, <i>ársēn</i>, Skt. <i>r̥ṣabhá</i>- ‘bull’). IEW 336, EIEC 363, NIL 584 ff. → [37], [291], [396].

393. ‘daughter-in-law’: *<i>snuso</i>- (: Skt. <i>snuṣā´</i>, Gk. <i>nuós</i>, Arm. <i>now</i>, Lat. <i>nurus</i>, OHG <i>snur</i>, <i>snora</i>, ORuss. <i>snъxa</i>). IEW 978, EIEC 148, NIL 625 f.

394. ‘father-/mother-in-law’: ‘father-’ *<i>su̯ek̑uro</i>- (: Skt. <i>śváśura</i>-, YAv. <i>xᵛasura</i>-, Gk. <i>hekurós</i>, Lat. <i>socer</i>, OE <i>swēor</i>, Lith. <i>šẽšuras</i>, RCS <i>svekrъ</i>, Arm. <i>skesrayr</i>); ‘mother-’ *<i>su̯ek̑ruH</i>- (: Skt. <i>śvaśrū́</i>-, Lat. <i>socur</i>, Goth. <i>swaihro</i>, Welsh <i>chwegr</i>, OCS <i>svekry</i>; Gk. <i>hekurā´</i>, Arm. <i>skesowr</i>). IEW 1043 f., EIEC 85, 195 f., 386 f., NIL 672 ff.

395. ‘sister’: *<i>su̯esor</i>- (: Skt. <i>svásar</i>-, YAv. <i>xᵛaŋhar</i>-, Gk. <i>éor</i> ‘female relative, niece, daughter’, Arm. <i>k‘oyr</i>, Lat. <i>soror</i>, OIr. <i>siur</i>, Welsh <i>chwaer</i>, Goth. <i>swistar</i>, Toch. A <i>ṣar</i>, B <i>ṣer</i>, OCS <i>sestra</i>, Lith. <i>sesuõ</i>, probably Alb. <i>vájzë</i>). IEW 1051, EIEC 521, NIL 680 ff.

396. ‘male, male animal’: *<i>u̯ers</i>- (: Skt. <i>vŕ̥ṣan</i>-, Lat. <i>verrēs</i> ‘boar’, Toch. A <i>kayurṣ</i>, B <i>kaurṣe</i> ‘bull’, YAv. <i>varǝšna</i>-, Lith. <i>ver˜šis</i> ‘calf’). IEW 81, EIEC 363, NIL 722 ff. → [37], [291], [392].

397. ‘iron’: *<i>īsarno</i>- (: OIr. <i>íarn</i>, Goth. <i>eisarn</i>, OHG OS ON <i>īsarn</i>). IEW 299 ff., EIEC 313 f.

398. ‘grandmother’: *<i>h₂en</i>- (: Hitt. <i>ḫanna</i>-, OHG <i>ana</i>, Arm. <i>han</i>). IEW 36 f., EIEC 238 f.

399. ‘husband’s sister’: *<i>g̑l̥H</i>- (: Gk. <i>gálōs</i>, Lat. <i>glōs</i>, OCS <i>zъlъva</i>, Arm. <i>tal</i> (with <i>t</i>-usually explained as taken from <i>taygr</i> ‘husband’s brother’). IEW 367, EIEC 521 f.

400. ‘diminish, perish’: *<i>mei̯H</i>- (: Skt. <i>minā´ti</i> ‘damages’, Gk. <i>minútʰō</i>, Lat. <i>minuere</i>, -<i>ō</i>). LIV 427, IEW 711.

401. ‘protect, herd’: *<i>peh₂(i)</i>- (: Hitt. <i>paḫḫašmi</i>, Lat. <i>pāscere</i>, -<i>ō</i>, Skt. <i>pā´ti</i>, Av. <i>pāiti</i>, Toch. B <i>paskenträ</i>, OCS <i>pasǫ</i>, <i>pasti</i>). LIV 460, IEW 787, 839.
